{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="188" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="195" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}" class="Module">plfa.part3.Denotational</a> <a id="219" class="Keyword">where</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
The lambda calculus is a language about _functions_, that is, mappings
from input to output. In computing we often think of such
mappings as being carried out by a sequence of
operations that transform an input into an output.  But
functions can also be represented as data. For example, one
can tabulate a function, that is, create a table where each row has
two entries, an input and the corresponding output for the function.
Function application is then the process of looking up the row for
a given input and reading off the output.

We shall create a semantics for the untyped lambda calculus based on
this idea of functions-as-tables. However, there are two difficulties
that arise. First, functions often have an infinite domain, so it
would seem that we would need infinitely long tables to represent
functions. Second, in the lambda calculus, functions can be applied to
functions. They can even be applied to themselves! So it would seem
that the tables would contain cycles. One might start to worry that
advanced techniques are necessary to address these issues, but
fortunately this is not the case!

The first problem, of functions with infinite domains, is solved by
observing that in the execution of a terminating program, each lambda
abstraction will only be applied to a finite number of distinct
arguments. (We come back later to discuss diverging programs.) This
observation is another way of looking at Dana Scott's insight that
only continuous functions are needed to model the lambda calculus.

The second problem, that of self-application, is solved by relaxing
the way in which we lookup an argument in a function's table.
Naively, one would look in the table for a row in which the input
entry exactly matches the argument. In the case of self-application,
this would require the table to contain a copy of itself. Impossible!
(At least, it is impossible if we want to build tables using inductive
data type definitions, which indeed we do.)  Instead it is sufficient
to find an input such that every row of the input appears as a row of
the argument (that is, the input is a subset of the argument).  In the
case of self-application, the table only needs to contain a smaller
copy of itself, which is fine.

With these two observations in hand, it is straightforward to write
down a denotational semantics of the lambda calculus.

## Values

The `Value` data type represents a finite portion of a function.  We
think of a value as a finite set of pairs that represent input-output
mappings. The `Value` data type represents the set as a binary tree
whose internal nodes are the union operator and whose leaves represent
either a single mapping or the empty set.

  * The âŠ¥ value provides no information about the computation.

  * A value of the form `v â†¦ w` is a single input-output mapping, from
    input `v` to output `w`.

  * A value of the form `v âŠ” w` is a function that maps inputs to
    outputs according to both `v` and `w`.  Think of it as taking the
    union of the two sets.

The `âŠ‘` relation adapts the familiar notion of subset to the Value data
type. This relation plays the key role in enabling self-application.
There are two rules that are specific to functions, `âŠ‘-fun` and `âŠ‘-dist`,
which we discuss below.

  <a id="_âŠ‘_.âŠ‘-trans"></a><a id="4756" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#4756" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-trans</a> <a id="4764" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="4766" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="4768" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="4769" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4769" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="4771" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4771" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="4773" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4773" class="Bound">w</a><a id="4774" class="Symbol">}</a>

    <a id="4792" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="4794" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#4771" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="4796" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="4798" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4773" class="Bound">w</a>

    <a id="4816" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="4818" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#4769" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="4820" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="4822" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4773" class="Bound">w</a>

    <a id="4905" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="4907" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="4908" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#4838" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="4910" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="4912" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4840" class="Bound">w</a><a id="4913" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="4915" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="4917" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="4918" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4842" class="Bound">vâ€²</a> <a id="4921" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="4923" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4845" class="Bound">wâ€²</a><a id="4925" class="Symbol">)</a>

</pre>{% endraw %}

The first five rules are straightforward.
The rule `âŠ‘-fun` captures when it is OK to match a higher-order argument
`vâ€² â†¦ wâ€²` to a table entry whose input is `v â†¦ w`.  Considering a
call to the higher-order argument. It is OK to pass a larger argument
than expected, so `v` can be larger than `vâ€²`. Also, it is OK to
disregard some of the output, so `w` can be smaller than `wâ€²`.
The rule `âŠ‘-dist` says that if you have two entries for the same input,
then you can combine them into a single entry and joins the two
outputs.

The `âŠ‘` relation is reflexive.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="âŠ‘-refl"></a><a id="5596" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a> <a id="5603" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5605" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="5607" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="5608" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5608" class="Bound">v</a><a id="5609" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="5611" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="5613" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5608" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="5615" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="5617" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5608" class="Bound">v</a>
<a id="5619" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a> <a id="5626" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="5627" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a><a id="5628" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="5630" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="5632" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4501" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-bot</a>
<a id="5638" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a> <a id="5645" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="5646" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5646" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="5648" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="5650" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5650" class="Bound">vâ€²</a><a id="5652" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="5654" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="5656" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4827" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-fun</a> <a id="5662" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a> <a id="5669" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a>
<a id="5676" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a> <a id="5683" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="5684" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5684" class="Bound">vâ‚</a> <a id="5687" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="5689" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5689" class="Bound">vâ‚‚</a><a id="5691" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="5693" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="5695" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4526" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-conj-L</a> <a id="5704" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="5705" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4610" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-conj-R1</a> <a id="5715" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a><a id="5721" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="5723" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="5724" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4683" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-conj-R2</a> <a id="5734" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a><a id="5740" class="Symbol">)</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
The `âŠ”` operation is monotonic with respect to `âŠ‘`, that is, given two
larger values it produces a larger value.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="âŠ”âŠ‘âŠ”"></a><a id="5865" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#5865" class="Function">âŠ”âŠ‘âŠ”</a> <a id="5869" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5871" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="5873" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="5874" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5874" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="5876" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5876" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="5878" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5878" class="Bound">vâ€²</a> <a id="5881" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5881" class="Bound">wâ€²</a><a id="5883" class="Symbol">}</a>
  <a id="5887" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="5889" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#5874" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="5891" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="5893" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5878" class="Bound">vâ€²</a>  <a id="5897" class="Symbol">â†’</a>  <a id="5900" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5876" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="5902" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="5904" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5881" class="Bound">wâ€²</a>
    <a id="5911" class="Comment">-----------------------</a>
  <a id="5937" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="5939" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="5940" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#5874" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="5942" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="5944" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5876" class="Bound">w</a><a id="5945" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="5947" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="5949" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="5950" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5878" class="Bound">vâ€²</a> <a id="5953" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="5955" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5881" class="Bound">wâ€²</a><a id="5957" class="Symbol">)</a>

</pre>{% endraw %}
The `âŠ‘-dist` rule can be used to combine two entries even when the
input values are not identical. One can first combine the two inputs
using âŠ” and then apply the `âŠ‘-dist` rule to obtain the following
property.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="âŠ”â†¦âŠ”-dist"></a><a id="6231" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#6231" class="Function">âŠ”â†¦âŠ”-dist</a> <a id="6240" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="6242" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="6244" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6244" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="6246" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6246" class="Bound">vâ€²</a> <a id="6249" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6249" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="6251" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6251" class="Bound">wâ€²</a> <a id="6254" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="6256" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a><a id="6261" class="Symbol">}</a>
  <a id="6265" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="6267" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="6268" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#6244" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="6270" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="6272" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6246" class="Bound">vâ€²</a><a id="6274" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="6276" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="6278" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="6279" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6249" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="6281" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="6283" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6251" class="Bound">wâ€²</a><a id="6285" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="6287" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="6289" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="6290" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6244" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="6292" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="6294" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6249" class="Bound">w</a><a id="6295" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="6297" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="6299" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="6300" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6246" class="Bound">vâ€²</a> <a id="6303" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="6305" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6251" class="Bound">wâ€²</a><a id="6307" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="6309" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#6231" class="Function">âŠ”â†¦âŠ”-dist</a> <a id="6318" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="6320" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4756" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-trans</a> <a id="6328" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4930" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-dist</a> <a id="6335" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="6336" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5865" class="Function">âŠ”âŠ‘âŠ”</a> <a id="6340" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="6341" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4827" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-fun</a> <a id="6347" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="6348" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4610" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-conj-R1</a> <a id="6358" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a><a id="6364" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="6366" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a><a id="6372" class="Symbol">)</a>
                            <a id="6402" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="6403" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#4827" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-fun</a> <a id="6409" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="6410" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4683" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-conj-R2</a> <a id="6420" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a><a id="6426" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="6428" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a><a id="6434" class="Symbol">))</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
<!--
 [PLW: above might read more nicely if we introduce inequational reasoning.]
 -->

If the join `u âŠ” v` is less than another value `w`,
then both `u` and `v` are less than `w`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="âŠ”âŠ‘-invL"></a><a id="6628" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#6628" class="Function">âŠ”âŠ‘-invL</a> <a id="6636" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="6638" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="6640" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6640" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="6642" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6642" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="6644" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6644" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="6646" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="6648" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a><a id="6653" class="Symbol">}</a>
  <a id="6657" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="6659" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#6640" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="6661" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="6663" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6642" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="6665" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="6667" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#6644" class="Bound">w</a>
    <a id="6673" class="Comment">---------</a>

## Environments

An environment gives meaning to the free variables in a term by
mapping variables to values.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="Env"></a><a id="7246" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="7250" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="7252" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3153" class="Datatype">Context</a> <a id="7260" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="7262" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>
<a id="7266" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="7270" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7270" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="7272" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="7274" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="7276" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="7277" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7277" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="7279" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="7281" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7270" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="7283" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3521" class="Datatype Operator">âˆ‹</a> <a id="7285" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a><a id="7286" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="7288" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="7290" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
We have the empty environment, and we can extend an environment.
{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="`âˆ…"></a><a id="7370" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#7370" class="Function">`âˆ…</a> <a id="7373" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="7375" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="7379" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3175" class="InductiveConstructor">âˆ…</a>

<a id="7388" class="Keyword">infixl</a> <a id="7395" class="Number">5</a> <a id="7397" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#7403" class="Function Operator">_`,_</a>

<a id="7446" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="7447" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#7447" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="7449" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7403" class="Function Operator">`,</a> <a id="7452" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7452" class="Bound">v</a><a id="7453" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="7455" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3557" class="InductiveConstructor">Z</a> <a id="7457" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="7459" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7452" class="Bound">v</a>
<a id="7461" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="7462" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#7462" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="7464" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7403" class="Function Operator">`,</a> <a id="7467" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7467" class="Bound">v</a><a id="7468" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="7470" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="7471" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3602" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">S</a> <a id="7473" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7473" class="Bound">x</a><a id="7474" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="7476" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="7478" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7462" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="7480" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7473" class="Bound">x</a>

We can recover the previous environment from an extended environment,
and the last value. Putting them together again takes us back to where we started.

We extend the `âŠ‘` relation point-wise to environments with the
following definition.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="_`âŠ‘_"></a><a id="8066" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#8066" class="Function Operator">_`âŠ‘_</a> <a id="8071" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8073" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="8075" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="8076" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8076" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="8077" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="8079" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8081" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="8085" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8076" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="8087" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8089" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="8093" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8076" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="8095" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8097" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>
<a id="8101" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#8066" class="Function Operator">_`âŠ‘_</a> <a id="8106" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="8107" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8107" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="8108" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="8110" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8110" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="8112" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8112" class="Bound">Î´</a> <a id="8114" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="8116" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="8118" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8119" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8119" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8121" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8123" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8107" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="8125" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3521" class="Datatype Operator">âˆ‹</a> <a id="8127" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a><a id="8128" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8130" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8132" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8110" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="8134" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8119" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8136" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="8138" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8112" class="Bound">Î´</a> <a id="8140" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8119" class="Bound">x</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
We define a bottom environment and a join operator on environments,
which takes the point-wise join of their values.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="`âŠ¥"></a><a id="8269" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#8269" class="Function">`âŠ¥</a> <a id="8272" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8274" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="8276" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="8277" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8277" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="8278" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="8280" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8282" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="8286" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8277" class="Bound">Î“</a>
<a id="8288" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#8269" class="Function">`âŠ¥</a> <a id="8291" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8291" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8293" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="8295" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a>

<a id="_`âŠ”_"></a><a id="8298" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#8298" class="Function Operator">_`âŠ”_</a> <a id="8303" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8305" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="8307" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="8308" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8308" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="8309" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="8311" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8313" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="8317" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8308" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="8319" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8321" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="8325" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8308" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="8327" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8329" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="8333" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8308" class="Bound">Î“</a>
<a id="8335" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8336" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#8336" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="8338" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8298" class="Function Operator">`âŠ”</a> <a id="8341" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8341" class="Bound">Î´</a><a id="8342" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8344" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8344" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8346" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="8348" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8336" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="8350" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8344" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8352" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="8354" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8341" class="Bound">Î´</a> <a id="8356" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8344" class="Bound">x</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
The `âŠ‘-refl`, `âŠ‘-conj-R1`, and `âŠ‘-conj-R2` rules lift to environments.  So
the join of two environments `Î³` and `Î´` is greater than the first
environment `Î³` or the second environment `Î´`.

<a id="âŠ‘-env-conj-R1"></a><a id="8628" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#8628" class="Function">âŠ‘-env-conj-R1</a> <a id="8642" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8644" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="8646" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="8647" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8647" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="8648" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="8650" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8652" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8653" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8653" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="8655" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8657" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="8661" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8647" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="8662" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8664" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8666" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8667" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8667" class="Bound">Î´</a> <a id="8669" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8671" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="8675" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8647" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="8676" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8678" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8680" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8653" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="8682" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8066" class="Function Operator">`âŠ‘</a> <a id="8685" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8686" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8653" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="8688" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8298" class="Function Operator">`âŠ”</a> <a id="8691" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8667" class="Bound">Î´</a><a id="8692" class="Symbol">)</a>

## Denotational Semantics

We define the semantics with a judgment of the form `Ï âŠ¢ M â†“ v`,
where `Ï` is the environment, `M` the program, and `v` is a result value.
For readers familiar with big-step semantics, this notation will feel
quite natural, but don't let the similarity fool you.  There are
subtle but important differences! So here is the definition of the
semantics, which we discuss in detail in the following paragraphs.

    <a id="9929" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="9931" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#9862" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="9933" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="9935" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9874" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="9937" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">â†“</a> <a id="9939" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9878" class="Bound">w</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
Consider the rule for lambda abstractions, `â†¦-intro`.  It says that a
lambda abstraction results in a single-entry table that maps the input
`v` to the output `w`, provided that evaluating the body in an
environment with `v` bound to its parameter produces the output `w`.
As a simple example of this rule, we can see that the identity function
maps `âŠ¥` to `âŠ¥` and also that it maps `âŠ¥ â†¦ âŠ¥` to `âŠ¥ â†¦ âŠ¥`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="denot-id1"></a><a id="10385" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#10385" class="Function">denot-id1</a> <a id="10395" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="10397" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="10399" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="10400" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#10400" class="Bound">Î³</a><a id="10401" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="10403" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="10405" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#10400" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="10407" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="10409" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#10354" class="Function">id</a> <a id="10412" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">â†“</a> <a id="10414" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a> <a id="10416" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="10418" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a>

<a id="denot-id2"></a><a id="10445" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#10445" class="Function">denot-id2</a> <a id="10455" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="10457" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="10459" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="10460" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#10460" class="Bound">Î³</a><a id="10461" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="10463" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="10465" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#10460" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="10467" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="10469" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#10354" class="Function">id</a> <a id="10472" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">â†“</a> <a id="10474" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="10475" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a> <a id="10477" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="10479" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a><a id="10480" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="10482" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="10484" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="10485" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a> <a id="10487" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="10489" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a><a id="10490" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="10492" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#10445" class="Function">denot-id2</a> <a id="10502" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="10504" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9555" class="InductiveConstructor">â†¦-intro</a> <a id="10512" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9358" class="InductiveConstructor">var</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
Of course, we will need tables with many rows to capture the meaning
of lambda abstractions. These can be constructed using the `âŠ”-intro`
rule.  If term M (typically a lambda abstraction) can produce both
tables `v` and `w`, then it produces the combined table `v âŠ” w`. One
can take an operational view of the rules `â†¦-intro` and `âŠ”-intro` by
imagining that when an interpreter first comes to a lambda
abstraction, it pre-evaluates the function on a bunch of randomly
chosen arguments, using many instances of the rule `â†¦-intro`, and then
joins them into a big table using many instances of the rule `âŠ”-intro`.
In the following we show that the identity function produces a table
containing both of the previous results, `âŠ¥ â†¦ âŠ¥` and
`(âŠ¥ â†¦ âŠ¥) â†¦ (âŠ¥ â†¦ âŠ¥)`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="denot-id3"></a><a id="11280" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#11280" class="Function">denot-id3</a> <a id="11290" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="11292" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7370" class="Function">`âˆ…</a> <a id="11295" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="11297" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#10354" class="Function">id</a> <a id="11300" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">â†“</a> <a id="11302" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11303" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a> <a id="11305" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="11307" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a><a id="11308" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="11310" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="11312" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11313" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a> <a id="11315" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="11317" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a><a id="11318" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="11320" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="11322" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11323" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a> <a id="11325" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="11327" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a><a id="11328" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="11330" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#11280" class="Function">denot-id3</a> <a id="11340" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="11342" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9734" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ”-intro</a> <a id="11350" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#10385" class="Function">denot-id1</a> <a id="11360" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#10445" class="Function">denot-id2</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
We most often think of the judgment `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v` as taking the
environment `Î³` and term `M` as input, producing the result `v`.  However,
it is worth emphasizing that the semantics is a _relation_.  The above
results for the identity function show that the same environment and
term can be mapped to different results. However, the results for a
given `Î³` and `M` are not _too_ different, they are all finite
approximations of the same function. Perhaps a better way of thinking
about the judgment `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v` is that the `Î³`, `M`, and `v` are all inputs
and the semantics either confirms or denies whether `v` is an accurate
partial description of the result of `M` in environment `Î³`.

Next we consider the meaning of function application as given by the
`â†¦-elim` rule. In the premise of the rule we have that `L` maps `v` to
`w`. So if `M` produces `v`, then the application of `L` to `M`
produces `w`.

As an example of function application and the `â†¦-elim` rule, we apply
the identity function to itself.  Indeed, we have both that
`âˆ… âŠ¢ id â†“ (u â†¦ u) â†¦ (u â†¦ u)` and also `âˆ… âŠ¢ id â†“ (u â†¦ u)`, so we can
apply the rule `â†¦-elim`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="id-app-id"></a><a id="12509" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#12509" class="Function">id-app-id</a> <a id="12519" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="12521" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="12523" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="12524" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#12524" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="12526" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="12528" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a><a id="12533" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="12535" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="12537" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7370" class="Function">`âˆ…</a> <a id="12540" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="12542" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#10354" class="Function">id</a> <a id="12545" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4442" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Â·</a> <a id="12547" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#10354" class="Function">id</a> <a id="12550" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">â†“</a> <a id="12552" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12553" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#12524" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="12555" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="12557" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#12524" class="Bound">u</a><a id="12558" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="12560" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#12509" class="Function">id-app-id</a> <a id="12570" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="12571" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#12571" class="Bound">u</a><a id="12572" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="12574" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12576" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9433" class="InductiveConstructor">â†¦-elim</a> <a id="12583" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12584" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9555" class="InductiveConstructor">â†¦-intro</a> <a id="12592" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9358" class="InductiveConstructor">var</a><a id="12595" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="12597" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12598" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9555" class="InductiveConstructor">â†¦-intro</a> <a id="12606" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9358" class="InductiveConstructor">var</a><a id="12609" class="Symbol">)</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
Next we revisit the Church numeral two: `Î» f. Î» u. (f (f u))`.
This function has two parameters: a function `f` and an arbitrary value
`u`, and it applies `f` twice. So `f` must map `u` to some value, which
we'll name `v`. Then for the second application,
`f` must map `v` to some value. Let's name it `w`. So the function's
table must include two entries, both `u â†¦ v` and `v â†¦ w`. For each
application of the table, we extract the appropriate entry from it
using the `sub` rule.  In particular, we use the âŠ‘-conj-R1 and
âŠ‘-conj-R2 to select `u â†¦ v` and `v â†¦ w`, respectively, from the table
`u â†¦ v âŠ” v â†¦ w`. So the meaning of twoá¶œ is that it takes this table
and parameter `u`, and it returns `w`.  Indeed we derive this as
follows.

  <a id="13520" class="Keyword">where</a> <a id="13526" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#13526" class="Function">lt1</a> <a id="13530" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13532" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#13440" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="13534" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="13536" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#13443" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="13538" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="13540" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#13437" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="13542" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="13544" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#13440" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="13546" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="13548" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#13440" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="13550" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="13552" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#13443" class="Bound">w</a>

Next we have a classic example of self application: `Î” = Î»x. (x x)`.
The input value for `x` needs to be a table, and it needs to have an
entry that maps a smaller version of itself, call it `v`, to some value
`w`. So the input value looks like `v â†¦ w âŠ” v`. Of course, then the
output of `Î”` is `w`. The derivation is given below.  The first occurrences
of `x` evaluates to `v â†¦ w`, the second occurrence of `x` evaluates to `v`,
and then the result of the application is `w`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="Î”"></a><a id="14173" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#14173" class="Function">Î”</a> <a id="14175" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="14177" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3175" class="InductiveConstructor">âˆ…</a> <a id="14179" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#4294" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="14181" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a>
<a id="14183" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#14173" class="Function">Î”</a> <a id="14185" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="14187" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14188" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4382" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Æ›</a> <a id="14190" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14191" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#5111" class="Function Operator">#</a> <a id="14193" class="Number">0</a><a id="14194" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="14196" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#4442" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Â·</a> <a id="14198" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14199" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#5111" class="Function Operator">#</a> <a id="14201" class="Number">0</a><a id="14202" class="Symbol">))</a>

<a id="denot-Î”"></a><a id="14206" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#14206" class="Function">denot-Î”</a> <a id="14214" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="14216" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="14218" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="14219" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#14219" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="14221" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#14221" class="Bound">w</a><a id="14222" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="14224" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="14226" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7370" class="Function">`âˆ…</a> <a id="14229" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="14231" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#14173" class="Function">Î”</a> <a id="14233" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">â†“</a> <a id="14235" class="Symbol">((</a><a id="14237" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#14219" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="14239" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="14241" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#14221" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="14243" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="14245" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#14219" class="Bound">v</a><a id="14246" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="14248" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="14250" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#14221" class="Bound">w</a><a id="14251" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="14253" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#14206" class="Function">denot-Î”</a> <a id="14261" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="14263" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9555" class="InductiveConstructor">â†¦-intro</a> <a id="14271" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14272" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9433" class="InductiveConstructor">â†¦-elim</a> <a id="14279" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14280" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9849" class="InductiveConstructor">sub</a> <a id="14284" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9358" class="InductiveConstructor">var</a> <a id="14288" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14289" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4610" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-conj-R1</a> <a id="14299" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a><a id="14305" class="Symbol">))</a>
                          <a id="14334" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14335" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#9849" class="InductiveConstructor">sub</a> <a id="14339" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9358" class="InductiveConstructor">var</a> <a id="14343" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14344" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4683" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ‘-conj-R2</a> <a id="14354" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a><a id="14360" class="Symbol">)))</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
One might worry whether this semantics can deal with diverging
programs.  The `âŠ¥` value and the `âŠ¥-intro` rule provide a way to handle
them. (The `âŠ¥-intro` rule is also what enables Î² reduction on
non-terminating arguments.)  The classic `Î©` program is a particularly
simple program that diverges. It applies `Î”` to itself. The semantics
assigns to `Î©` the meaning `âŠ¥`. There are several ways to derive this, we
shall start with one that makes use of the `âŠ”-intro` rule.  First,
`denot-Î”` tells us that `Î”` evaluates to `((âŠ¥ â†¦ âŠ¥) âŠ” âŠ¥) â†¦ âŠ¥`
(choose `vâ‚ = vâ‚‚ = âŠ¥`).  Next, `Î”` also evaluates to `âŠ¥ â†¦ âŠ¥` by use of
`â†¦-intro` and `âŠ¥-intro` and to `âŠ¥` by `âŠ¥-intro`. As we saw previously,
whenever we can show that a program evaluates to two values, we can apply
`âŠ”-intro` to join them together, so `Î”` evaluates to `(âŠ¥ â†¦ âŠ¥) âŠ” âŠ¥`. This
matches the input of the first occurrence of `Î”`, so we can conclude that
the result of the application is `âŠ¥`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="Î©"></a><a id="15315" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#15315" class="Function">Î©</a> <a id="15317" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="15319" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3175" class="InductiveConstructor">âˆ…</a> <a id="15321" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#4294" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="15323" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a>
<a id="15325" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#15315" class="Function">Î©</a> <a id="15327" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="15329" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#14173" class="Function">Î”</a> <a id="15331" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4442" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Â·</a> <a id="15333" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#14173" class="Function">Î”</a>

<a id="denot-Î©"></a><a id="15336" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#15336" class="Function">denot-Î©</a> <a id="15344" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="15346" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7370" class="Function">`âˆ…</a> <a id="15349" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="15351" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#15315" class="Function">Î©</a> <a id="15353" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">â†“</a> <a id="15355" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a>
<a id="15357" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#15336" class="Function">denot-Î©</a> <a id="15365" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="15367" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9433" class="InductiveConstructor">â†¦-elim</a> <a id="15374" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#14206" class="Function">denot-Î”</a> <a id="15382" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="15383" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9734" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ”-intro</a> <a id="15391" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="15392" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9555" class="InductiveConstructor">â†¦-intro</a> <a id="15400" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9667" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥-intro</a><a id="15407" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="15409" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9667" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥-intro</a><a id="15416" class="Symbol">)</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
A shorter derivation of the same result is by just one use of the
`âŠ¥-intro` rule.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="denot-Î©&#39;"></a><a id="15510" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#15510" class="Function">denot-Î©&#39;</a> <a id="15519" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="15521" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7370" class="Function">`âˆ…</a> <a id="15524" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="15526" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#15315" class="Function">Î©</a> <a id="15528" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">â†“</a> <a id="15530" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a>
<a id="15532" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#15510" class="Function">denot-Î©&#39;</a> <a id="15541" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="15543" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9667" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥-intro</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
Just because one can derive `âˆ… âŠ¢ M â†“ âŠ¥` for some closed term `M` doesn't mean
that `M` necessarily diverges. There may be other derivations that
conclude with `M` producing some more informative value.  However, if
the only thing that a term evaluates to is `âŠ¥`, then it indeed diverges.

An attentive reader may have noticed a disconnect earlier in the way
we planned to solve the self-application problem and the actual
`â†¦-elim` rule for application. We said at the beginning that we would
relax the notion of table lookup, allowing an argument to match an
input entry if the argument is equal or greater than the input entry.
Instead, the `â†¦-elim` rule seems to require an exact match.  However,
because of the `sub` rule, application really does allow larger
arguments.

#### Exercise `denot-plusá¶œ` (practice)

What is a denotation for `plusá¶œ`? That is, find a value `v` (other than `âŠ¥`)
such that `âˆ… âŠ¢ plusá¶œ â†“ v`. Also, give the proof of `âˆ… âŠ¢ plusá¶œ â†“ v`
for your choice of `v`.

#### Exercise `denot-church` (recommended)

Church numerals are more general than natural numbers in that they
represent paths in a graph. The following `Path` predicate specifies
when a value of the form `f â†¦ a â†¦ b` represents a path from the
starting point `a` to the end point `b` in the graph of the function `f`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="17087" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="Path"></a><a id="17092" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#17092" class="Datatype">Path</a> <a id="17097" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17099" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="17100" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17100" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="17102" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17104" href="Agda.Builtin.Nat.html#165" class="Datatype">â„•</a><a id="17105" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="17107" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="17109" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a> <a id="17115" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="17117" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="17121" class="Keyword">where</a>
  <a id="Path.singleton"></a><a id="17129" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#17129" class="InductiveConstructor">singleton</a> <a id="17139" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17141" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="17143" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17143" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="17145" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17145" class="Bound">a</a><a id="17146" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="17148" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="17150" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17092" class="Datatype">Path</a> <a id="17155" class="Number">0</a> <a id="17157" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="17158" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17143" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="17160" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="17162" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17145" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="17164" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="17166" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17145" class="Bound">a</a><a id="17167" class="Symbol">)</a>
  <a id="Path.edge"></a><a id="17171" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#17171" class="InductiveConstructor">edge</a> <a id="17176" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17178" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="17180" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17180" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="17182" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17182" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="17184" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17184" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="17186" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17186" class="Bound">b</a> <a id="17188" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17188" class="Bound">c</a><a id="17189" class="Symbol">}</a>
     <a id="17196" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="17198" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#17092" class="Datatype">Path</a> <a id="17203" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17180" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="17205" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="17206" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17182" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="17208" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="17210" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17184" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="17212" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="17214" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17186" class="Bound">b</a><a id="17215" class="Symbol">)</a>
     <a id="17222" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="17224" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#17186" class="Bound">b</a> <a id="17226" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="17228" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17188" class="Bound">c</a> <a id="17230" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="17232" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17182" class="Bound">f</a>
     <a id="17239" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="17241" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#17092" class="Datatype">Path</a> <a id="17246" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="17247" href="Agda.Builtin.Nat.html#196" class="InductiveConstructor">suc</a> <a id="17251" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17180" class="Bound">n</a><a id="17252" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="17254" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="17255" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17182" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="17257" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="17259" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17184" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="17261" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="17263" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17188" class="Bound">c</a><a id="17264" class="Symbol">)</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
* A singleton path is of the form `f â†¦ a â†¦ a`.

* If there is a path from `a` to `b` and
  an edge from `b` to `c` in graph of `f`,
  then there is a path from `a` to `c`.

This exercise is to prove that if `f â†¦ a â†¦ b` is a path of length `n`,
then `f â†¦ a â†¦ b` is a meaning of the Church numeral `n`.

To fascilitate talking about arbitrary Church numerals, the following
`church` function builds the term for the nth Church numeral,
using the auxilliary function `apply-n`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="apply-n"></a><a id="17751" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#17751" class="Function">apply-n</a> <a id="17759" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17761" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="17762" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17762" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="17764" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17766" href="Agda.Builtin.Nat.html#165" class="Datatype">â„•</a><a id="17767" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="17769" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="17771" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3175" class="InductiveConstructor">âˆ…</a> <a id="17773" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#3191" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="17775" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a> <a id="17777" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#3191" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="17779" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a> <a id="17781" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#4294" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="17783" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a>

<a id="17804" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#17751" class="Function">apply-n</a> <a id="17812" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="17813" href="Agda.Builtin.Nat.html#196" class="InductiveConstructor">suc</a> <a id="17817" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17817" class="Bound">n</a><a id="17818" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="17820" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="17822" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#5111" class="Function Operator">#</a> <a id="17824" class="Number">1</a> <a id="17826" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#4442" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Â·</a> <a id="17828" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17751" class="Function">apply-n</a> <a id="17836" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17817" class="Bound">n</a>

<a id="church"></a><a id="17839" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#17839" class="Function">church</a> <a id="17846" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17848" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="17849" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17849" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="17851" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17853" href="Agda.Builtin.Nat.html#165" class="Datatype">â„•</a><a id="17854" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="17856" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="17858" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3175" class="InductiveConstructor">âˆ…</a> <a id="17860" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#4294" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="17862" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a>
<a id="17864" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#17839" class="Function">church</a> <a id="17871" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17871" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="17873" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="17875" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4382" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Æ›</a> <a id="17877" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#4382" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Æ›</a> <a id="17879" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17751" class="Function">apply-n</a> <a id="17887" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#17871" class="Bound">n</a> 
</pre>{% endraw %}
Prove the following theorem.

    denot-church : âˆ€{n v}
       â†’ Path n v
         -----------------
       â†’ `âˆ… âŠ¢ church n â†“ v

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="18028" class="Comment">-- Your code goes here</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
## Denotations and denotational equality

Next we define a notion of denotational equality based on the above
semantics. Its statement makes use of an if-and-only-if, which we
define as follows.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="_iff_"></a><a id="18256" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#18256" class="Function Operator">_iff_</a> <a id="18262" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="18264" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="18268" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18270" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="18274" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18276" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>
<a id="18280" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#18280" class="Bound">P</a> <a id="18282" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18256" class="Function Operator">iff</a> <a id="18286" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18286" class="Bound">Q</a> <a id="18288" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="18290" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="18291" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18280" class="Bound">P</a> <a id="18293" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18295" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18286" class="Bound">Q</a><a id="18296" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="18298" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Product.html#1162" class="Function Operator">Ã—</a> <a id="18300" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="18301" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18286" class="Bound">Q</a> <a id="18303" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18305" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18280" class="Bound">P</a><a id="18306" class="Symbol">)</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
Another way to view the denotational semantics is as a function that
maps a term to a relation from environments to values.  That is, the
_denotation_ of a term is a relation from environments to values.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="Denotation"></a><a id="18522" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#18522" class="Function">Denotation</a> <a id="18533" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="18535" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3153" class="Datatype">Context</a> <a id="18543" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18545" class="PrimitiveType">Setâ‚</a>
<a id="18550" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#18522" class="Function">Denotation</a> <a id="18561" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18561" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="18563" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="18565" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="18566" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="18570" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18561" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="18572" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18574" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a> <a id="18580" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18582" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a><a id="18585" class="Symbol">)</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
The following function â„° gives this alternative view of the semantics,
which really just amounts to changing the order of the parameters.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="â„°"></a><a id="18735" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#18735" class="Function">â„°</a> <a id="18737" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="18739" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="18741" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18741" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="18742" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="18744" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18746" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="18747" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18747" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="18749" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="18751" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18741" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="18753" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4294" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="18755" href="plfa.part2.Untyped.html#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a><a id="18756" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="18758" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18760" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18522" class="Function">Denotation</a> <a id="18771" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18741" class="Bound">Î“</a>
<a id="18773" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#18735" class="Function">â„°</a> <a id="18775" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18775" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="18777" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="18779" class="Symbol">Î»</a> <a id="18781" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18781" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="18783" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18783" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="18785" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18787" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18781" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="18789" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="18791" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18775" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="18793" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9304" class="Datatype Operator">â†“</a> <a id="18795" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18783" class="Bound">v</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
In general, two denotations are equal when they produce the same
values in the same environment.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="18904" class="Keyword">infix</a> <a id="18910" class="Number">3</a> <a id="18912" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#18917" class="Function Operator">_â‰ƒ_</a>

<a id="_â‰ƒ_"></a><a id="18917" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#18917" class="Function Operator">_â‰ƒ_</a> <a id="18921" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="18923" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="18925" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="18926" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18926" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="18927" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="18929" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18931" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="18932" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18522" class="Function">Denotation</a> <a id="18943" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18926" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="18944" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="18946" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18948" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="18949" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18522" class="Function">Denotation</a> <a id="18960" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18926" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="18961" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="18963" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="18965" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>
<a id="18969" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="18970" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#18917" class="Function Operator">_â‰ƒ_</a> <a id="18974" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="18975" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18975" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="18976" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="18978" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18978" class="Bound">Dâ‚</a> <a id="18981" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18981" class="Bound">Dâ‚‚</a><a id="18983" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="18985" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="18987" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="18988" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18988" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="18990" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="18992" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="18996" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18975" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="18997" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="18999" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="19001" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="19002" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#19002" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="19004" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="19006" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a><a id="19011" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="19013" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="19015" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18978" class="Bound">Dâ‚</a> <a id="19018" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18988" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="19020" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#19002" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="19022" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18256" class="Function Operator">iff</a> <a id="19026" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18981" class="Bound">Dâ‚‚</a> <a id="19029" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18988" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="19031" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#19002" class="Bound">v</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
Denotational equality is an equivalence relation.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="â‰ƒ-refl"></a><a id="19093" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#19093" class="Function">â‰ƒ-refl</a> <a id="19100" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="19102" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="19104" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="19105" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#19105" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="19107" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="19109" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3153" class="Datatype">Context</a><a id="19116" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="19118" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="19120" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="19121" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#19121" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="19123" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="19125" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#18522" class="Function">Denotation</a> <a id="19136" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#19105" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="19137" class="Symbol">}</a>

</pre>{% endraw %}
Two terms `M` and `N` are denotational equal when their denotations are
equal, that is, `â„° M â‰ƒ â„° N`.

The following submodule introduces equational reasoning for the `â‰ƒ`
relation.

## Road map for the following chapters

The subsequent chapters prove that the denotational semantics has
several desirable properties. First, we prove that the semantics is
compositional, i.e., that the denotation of a term is a function of
the denotations of its subterms. To do this we shall prove equations
of the following shape.

    â„° (` x) â‰ƒ ...
    â„° (Æ› M) â‰ƒ ... â„° M ...
    â„° (M Â· N) â‰ƒ ... â„° M ... â„° N ...

The compositionality property is not trivial because the semantics we
have defined includes three rules that are not syntax directed:
`âŠ¥-intro`, `âŠ”-intro`, and `sub`. The above equations suggest that the
dentoational semantics can be defined as a recursive function, and
indeed, we give such a definition and prove that it is equivalent to
â„°.

Next we investigate whether the denotational semantics and the
reduction semantics are equivalent. Recall that the job of a language
semantics is to describe the observable behavior of a given program
`M`. For the lambda calculus there are several choices that one can
make, but they usually boil down to a single bit of information:

  * divergence: the program `M` executes forever.
  * termination: the program `M` halts.

We can characterize divergence and termination in terms of reduction.

  * divergence: `Â¬ (M â€”â†  Æ› N)` for any term `N`.
  * termination: `M â€”â†  Æ› N` for some term `N`.

We can also characterize divergence and termination using denotations.

  * divergence: `Â¬ (âˆ… âŠ¢ M â†“ v â†¦ w)` for any `v` and `w`.
  * termination: `âˆ… âŠ¢ M â†“ v â†¦ w` for some `v` and `w`.

Alternatively, we can use the denotation function `â„°`.

  * divergence: `Â¬ (â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N))` for any term `N`.
  * termination: `â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N)` for some term `N`.

So the question is whether the reduction semantics and denotational
semantics are equivalent.

    (âˆƒ N. M â€”â†  Æ› N)  iff  (âˆƒ N. â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N))

We address each direction of the equivalence in the second and third
chapters. In the second chapter we prove that reduction to a lambda
abstraction implies denotational equality to a lambda
abstraction. This property is called the _soundness_ in the
literature.

    M â€”â†  Æ› N  implies  â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N)

In the third chapter we prove that denotational equality to a lambda
abstraction implies reduction to a lambda abstraction. This property
is called _adequacy_ in the literature.

    â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N)  implies M â€”â†  Æ› Nâ€² for some Nâ€²

The fourth chapter applies the results of the three preceeding
chapters (compositionality, soundness, and adequacy) to prove that
denotational equality implies a property called _contextual
equivalence_. This property is important because it justifies the use
of denotational equality in proving the correctness of program
transformations such as performance optimizations.

The proofs of all of these properties rely on some basic results about
the denotational semantics, which we establish in the rest of this
chapter.  We start with some lemmas about renaming, which are quite
similar to the renaming lemmas that we have seen in previous chapters.
We conclude with a proof of an important inversion lemma for the
less-than relation regarding function values.


## Renaming preserves denotations

We shall prove that renaming variables, and changing the environment
accordingly, preserves the meaning of a term. We generalize the
renaming lemma to allow the values in the new environment to be the
same or larger than the original values. This generalization is useful
in proving that reduction implies denotational equality.

As before, we need an extension lemma to handle the case where we
proceed underneath a lambda abstraction. Suppose that `Ï` is a
renaming that maps variables in `Î³` into variables with equal or
larger values in `Î´`. This lemmas says that extending the renaming
producing a renaming `ext r` that maps `Î³ , v` to `Î´ , v`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="ext-âŠ‘"></a><a id="24653" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#24653" class="Function">ext-âŠ‘</a> <a id="24659" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="24661" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="24663" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="24664" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24664" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="24666" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24666" class="Bound">Î”</a> <a id="24668" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24668" class="Bound">v</a><a id="24669" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="24671" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="24672" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24672" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="24674" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="24676" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="24680" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24664" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="24681" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="24683" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="24684" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24684" class="Bound">Î´</a> <a id="24686" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="24688" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="24692" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24666" class="Bound">Î”</a><a id="24693" class="Symbol">}</a>
  <a id="24697" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="24699" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="24700" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#24700" class="Bound">Ï</a> <a id="24702" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="24704" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Substitution.md %}{% raw %}#2192" class="Function">Rename</a> <a id="24711" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24664" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="24713" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24666" class="Bound">Î”</a><a id="24714" class="Symbol">)</a>
  <a id="24718" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="24720" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#24672" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="24722" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8066" class="Function Operator">`âŠ‘</a> <a id="24725" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="24726" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24684" class="Bound">Î´</a> <a id="24728" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Function.html#1099" class="Function Operator">âˆ˜</a> <a id="24730" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24700" class="Bound">Ï</a><a id="24731" class="Symbol">)</a>
    <a id="24737" class="Comment">------------------------------</a>
  <a id="24770" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="24772" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="24773" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#24672" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="24775" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7403" class="Function Operator">`,</a> <a id="24778" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24668" class="Bound">v</a><a id="24779" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="24781" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#8066" class="Function Operator">`âŠ‘</a> <a id="24784" class="Symbol">((</a><a id="24786" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24684" class="Bound">Î´</a> <a id="24788" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7403" class="Function Operator">`,</a> <a id="24791" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24668" class="Bound">v</a><a id="24792" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="24794" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Function.html#1099" class="Function Operator">âˆ˜</a> <a id="24796" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#5925" class="Function">ext</a> <a id="24800" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24700" class="Bound">Ï</a><a id="24801" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="24803" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#24653" class="Function">ext-âŠ‘</a> <a id="24809" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24809" class="Bound">Ï</a> <a id="24811" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24811" class="Bound">lt</a> <a id="24814" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3557" class="InductiveConstructor">Z</a> <a id="24816" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="24818" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#5596" class="Function">âŠ‘-refl</a>
<a id="24825" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#24653" class="Function">ext-âŠ‘</a> <a id="24831" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24831" class="Bound">Ï</a> <a id="24833" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24833" class="Bound">lt</a> <a id="24836" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="24837" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3602" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">S</a> <a id="24839" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24839" class="Bound">nâ€²</a><a id="24841" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="24843" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="24845" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24833" class="Bound">lt</a> <a id="24848" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#24839" class="Bound">nâ€²</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
We proceed by cases on the de Bruijn index `n`.

* If it is `Z`, then we just need to show that `v â‰¡ v`, which we have by `refl`.

* If it is `S nâ€²`, then the goal simplifies to `Î³ nâ€² â‰¡ Î´ (Ï nâ€²)`,
  which is an instance of the premise.

Now for the renaming lemma. Suppose we have a renaming that maps
variables in `Î³` into variables with the same values in `Î´`.  If `M`
results in `v` when evaluated in environment `Î³`, then applying the
renaming to `M` produces a program that results in the same value `v` when
evaluated in `Î´`.
