   <a id="25841" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#9734" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ”-intro</a> <a id="25849" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="25850" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25393" class="Function">rename-pres</a> <a id="25862" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25816" class="Bound">Ï</a> <a id="25864" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25818" class="Bound">lt</a> <a id="25867" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25830" class="Bound">d</a><a id="25868" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="25870" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="25871" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25393" class="Function">rename-pres</a> <a id="25883" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25816" class="Bound">Ï</a> <a id="25885" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25818" class="Bound">lt</a> <a id="25888" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25832" class="Bound">dâ‚</a><a id="25890" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="25892" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#25393" class="Function">rename-pres</a> <a id="25904" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25904" class="Bound">Ï</a> <a id="25906" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25906" class="Bound">lt</a> <a id="25909" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="25910" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#9849" class="InductiveConstructor">sub</a> <a id="25914" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25914" class="Bound">d</a> <a id="25916" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25916" class="Bound">ltâ€²</a><a id="25919" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="25921" class="Symbol">=</a>
   <a id="25926" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#9849" class="InductiveConstructor">sub</a> <a id="25930" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="25931" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25393" class="Function">rename-pres</a> <a id="25943" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25904" class="Bound">Ï</a> <a id="25945" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25906" class="Bound">lt</a> <a id="25948" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25914" class="Bound">d</a><a id="25949" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="25951" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#25916" class="Bound">ltâ€²</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
The proof is by induction on the semantics of `M`.  As you can see, all
of the cases are trivial except the cases for variables and lambda.

* For a variable `x`, we make use of the premise to show that
  `Î³ x â‰¡ Î´ (Ï x)`.

* For a lambda abstraction, the induction hypothesis requires us to
  extend the renaming. We do so, and use the `ext-âŠ‘` lemma to show
  that the extended renaming maps variables to ones with equivalent
  values.


## Environment strengthening and identity renaming

We shall need a corollary of the renaming lemma that says that
replacing the environment with a larger one (a stronger one) does not
change whether a term `M` results in particular value `v`. In
particular, if `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v` and `Î³ âŠ‘ Î´`, then `Î´ âŠ¢ M â†“ v`.  What does
this have to do with renaming?  It's renaming with the identity
function.  We apply the renaming lemma with the identity renaming,
which gives us `Î´ âŠ¢ rename (Î» {A} x â†’ x) M â†“ v`, and then we apply the
`rename-id` lemma to obtain `Î´ âŠ¢ M â†“ v`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="âŠ‘-env"></a><a id="26962" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#26962" class="Function">âŠ‘-env</a> <a id="26968" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="26970" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="26972" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="26973" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#26973" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="26974" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="26976" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="26977" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#26977" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="26979" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="26981" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="26985" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#26973" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="26986" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="26988" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="26989" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#26989" class="Bound">Î´</a> <a id="26991" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="26993" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#7246" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="26997" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#26973" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="26998" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="27000" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="27001" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#27001" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="27003" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#27003" class="Bound">v</a><a id="27004" class="Symbol">}</a>

In the proof that substitution reflects denotations, in the case for
lambda abstraction, we use a minor variation of `âŠ‘-env`, in which just
the last element of the environment gets larger.

## Inversion of the less-than relation for functions

What can we deduce from knowing that a function `v â†¦ w` is less than
some value `u`?  What can we deduce about `u`? The answer to this
question is called the inversion property of less-than for functions.
This question is not easy to answer because of the `âŠ‘-dist` rule, which
relates a function on the left to a pair of functions on the right.
So `u` may include several functions that, as a group, relate to
`v â†¦ w`. Furthermore, because of the rules `âŠ‘-conj-R1` and `âŠ‘-conj-R2`,
there may be other values inside `u`, such as `âŠ¥`, that have nothing
to do with `v â†¦ w`. But in general, we can deduce that `u` includes
a collection of functions where the join of their domains is less
than `v` and the join of their codomains is greater than `w`.

To precisely state and prove this inversion property, we need to
define what it means for a value to _include_ a collection of values.
We also need to define how to compute the join of their domains and
codomains.


### Value membership and inclusion

Recall that we think of a value as a set of entries with the join
operator `v âŠ” w` acting like set union. The function value `v â†¦ w` and
bottom value `âŠ¥` constitute the two kinds of elements of the set.  (In
other contexts one can instead think of `âŠ¥` as the empty set, but here
we must think of it as an element.)  We write `u âˆˆ v` to say that `u` is
an element of `v`, as defined below.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="29124" class="Keyword">infix</a> <a id="29130" class="Number">5</a> <a id="29132" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#29137" class="Function Operator">_âˆˆ_</a>

<a id="_âˆˆ_"></a><a id="29137" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#29137" class="Function Operator">_âˆˆ_</a> <a id="29141" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="29143" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a> <a id="29149" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="29151" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a> <a id="29157" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="29159" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>
<a id="29163" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#29163" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="29165" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29137" class="Function Operator">âˆˆ</a> <a id="29167" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a> <a id="29169" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="29171" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29163" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="29173" href="Agda.Builtin.Equality.html#125" class="Datatype Operator">â‰¡</a> <a id="29175" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a>
<a id="29177" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#29177" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="29179" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29137" class="Function Operator">âˆˆ</a> <a id="29181" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29181" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="29183" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="29185" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29185" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="29187" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="29189" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29177" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="29191" href="Agda.Builtin.Equality.html#125" class="Datatype Operator">â‰¡</a> <a id="29193" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29181" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="29195" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="29197" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29185" class="Bound">w</a>
<a id="29199" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#29199" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="29201" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29137" class="Function Operator">âˆˆ</a> <a id="29203" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="29204" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29204" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="29206" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="29208" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29208" class="Bound">w</a><a id="29209" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="29211" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="29213" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29199" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="29215" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29137" class="Function Operator">âˆˆ</a> <a id="29217" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29204" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="29219" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Sum.Base.html#612" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ</a> <a id="29221" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29199" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="29223" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29137" class="Function Operator">âˆˆ</a> <a id="29225" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29208" class="Bound">w</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
So we can represent a collection of values simply as a value.  We
write `v âŠ† w` to say that all the elements of `v` are also in `w`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="29370" class="Keyword">infix</a> <a id="29376" class="Number">5</a> <a id="29378" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#29383" class="Function Operator">_âŠ†_</a>

<a id="_âŠ†_"></a><a id="29383" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#29383" class="Function Operator">_âŠ†_</a> <a id="29387" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="29389" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a> <a id="29395" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="29397" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a> <a id="29403" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="29405" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>
<a id="29409" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#29409" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="29411" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29383" class="Function Operator">âŠ†</a> <a id="29413" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29413" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="29415" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="29417" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="29419" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29419" class="Bound">u</a><a id="29420" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="29422" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="29424" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29419" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="29426" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29137" class="Function Operator">âˆˆ</a> <a id="29428" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29409" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="29430" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="29432" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29419" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="29434" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29137" class="Function Operator">âˆˆ</a> <a id="29436" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29413" class="Bound">w</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
The notions of membership and inclusion for values are closely related
to the less-than relation. They are narrower relations in that they
imply the less-than relation but not the other way around.

We shall also need some inversion principles for value inclusion.  If
the union of `u` and `v` is included in `w`, then of course both `u` and
`v` are each included in `w`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="âŠ”âŠ†-inv"></a><a id="30264" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#30264" class="Function">âŠ”âŠ†-inv</a> <a id="30271" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="30273" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="30275" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30275" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="30277" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30277" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="30279" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30279" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="30281" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="30283" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a><a id="30288" class="Symbol">}</a>
       <a id="30297" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="30299" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="30300" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#30275" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="30302" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4171" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="30304" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30277" class="Bound">v</a><a id="30305" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="30307" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29383" class="Function Operator">âŠ†</a> <a id="30309" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30279" class="Bound">w</a>
         <a id="30320" class="Comment">---------------</a>
       <a id="30343" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="30345" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#30275" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="30347" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29383" class="Function Operator">âŠ†</a> <a id="30349" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30279" class="Bound">w</a>  <a id="30352" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Product.html#1162" class="Function Operator">Ã—</a>  <a id="30355" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30277" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="30357" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29383" class="Function Operator">âŠ†</a> <a id="30359" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30279" class="Bound">w</a>

</pre>{% endraw %}
In our value representation, the function value `v â†¦ w` is both an
element and also a singleton set. So if `v â†¦ w` is a subset of `u`,
then `v â†¦ w` must be a member of `u`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="â†¦âŠ†â†’âˆˆ"></a><a id="30605" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#30605" class="Function">â†¦âŠ†â†’âˆˆ</a> <a id="30610" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="30612" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="30614" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30614" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="30616" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30616" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="30618" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30618" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="30620" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="30622" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a><a id="30627" class="Symbol">}</a>
     <a id="30634" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="30636" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#30614" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="30638" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="30640" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30616" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="30642" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29383" class="Function Operator">âŠ†</a> <a id="30644" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30618" class="Bound">u</a>
       <a id="30653" class="Comment">---------</a>
     <a id="30668" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="30670" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#30614" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="30672" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="30674" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30616" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="30676" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29137" class="Function Operator">âˆˆ</a> <a id="30678" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30618" class="Bound">u</a>

</pre>{% endraw %}

### Function values

To identify collections of functions, we define the following two
predicates. We write `Fun u` if `u` is a function value, that is, if
`u â‰¡ v â†¦ w` for some values `v` and `w`. We write `all-funs v` if all the elements
of `v` are functions.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="30974" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="Fun"></a><a id="30979" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#30979" class="Datatype">Fun</a> <a id="30983" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="30985" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a> <a id="30991" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="30993" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="30997" class="Keyword">where</a>
  <a id="Fun.fun"></a><a id="31005" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#31005" class="InductiveConstructor">fun</a> <a id="31009" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="31011" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="31013" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#31013" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="31015" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#31015" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="31017" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#31017" class="Bound">w</a><a id="31018" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="31020" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="31022" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#31013" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="31024" href="Agda.Builtin.Equality.html#125" class="Datatype Operator">â‰¡</a> <a id="31026" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="31027" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#31015" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="31029" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="31031" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#31017" class="Bound">w</a><a id="31032" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="31034" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="31036" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30979" class="Datatype">Fun</a> <a id="31040" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#31013" class="Bound">u</a>

The value `âŠ¥` is not a function.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="Â¬FunâŠ¥"></a><a id="31143" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#31143" class="Function">Â¬FunâŠ¥</a> <a id="31149" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="31151" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Relation.Nullary.html#535" class="Function Operator">Â¬</a> <a id="31153" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="31154" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#30979" class="Datatype">Fun</a> <a id="31158" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4129" class="InductiveConstructor">âŠ¥</a><a id="31159" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="31161" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#31143" class="Function">Â¬FunâŠ¥</a> <a id="31167" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="31168" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#31005" class="InductiveConstructor">fun</a> <a id="31172" class="Symbol">())</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
In our values-as-sets representation, our sets always include at least
one element. Thus, if all the elements are functions, there is at
least one that is a function.

### Domains and codomains

Returning to our goal, the inversion principle for less-than a
function, we want to show that `v â†¦ w âŠ‘ u` implies that `u` includes
a set of function values such that the join of their domains is less
than `v` and the join of their codomains is greater than `w`.

To this end we define the following `â¨†dom` and `â¨†cod` functions.  Given some
value `u` (that represents a set of entries), `â¨†dom u` returns the join of
their domains and `â¨†cod u` returns the join of their codomains.

We need just one property each for `â¨†dom` and `â¨†cod`.  Given a collection of
functions represented by value `u`, and an entry `v â†¦ w âˆˆ u`, we know
that `v` is included in the domain of `v`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="â†¦âˆˆâ†’âŠ†â¨†dom"></a><a id="32530" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#32530" class="Function">â†¦âˆˆâ†’âŠ†â¨†dom</a> <a id="32539" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="32541" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="32543" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#32543" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="32545" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#32545" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="32547" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#32547" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="32549" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="32551" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a><a id="32556" class="Symbol">}</a>
          <a id="32568" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="32570" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#31043" class="Function">all-funs</a> <a id="32579" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#32543" class="Bound">u</a>  <a id="32582" class="Symbol">â†’</a>  <a id="32585" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="32586" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#32545" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="32588" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4141" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">â†¦</a> <a id="32590" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#32547" class="Bound">w</a><a id="32591" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="32593" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29137" class="Function Operator">âˆˆ</a> <a id="32595" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#32543" class="Bound">u</a>
            <a id="32609" class="Comment">----------------------</a>
          <a id="32642" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="32644" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#32545" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="32646" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29383" class="Function Operator">âŠ†</a> <a id="32648" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#32151" class="Function">â¨†dom</a> <a id="32653" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#32543" class="Bound">u</a>

Regarding `â¨†cod`, suppose we have a collection of functions represented
by `u`, but all of them are just copies of `v â†¦ w`.  Then the `â¨†cod u` is
included in `w`.

</pre>{% endraw %}
With the `â¨†dom` and `â¨†cod` functions in hand, we can make precise the
conclusion of the inversion principle for functions, which we package
into the following predicate named `factor`. We say that `v â†¦ w`
_factors_ `u` into `uâ€²` if `uâ€²` is a included in `u`, if `uâ€²` contains only
functions, its domain is less than `v`, and its codomain is greater
than `w`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="factor"></a><a id="33793" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#33793" class="Function">factor</a> <a id="33800" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="33802" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="33803" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33803" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="33805" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="33807" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a><a id="33812" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="33814" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="33816" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="33817" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33817" class="Bound">uâ€²</a> <a id="33820" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="33822" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a><a id="33827" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="33829" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="33831" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="33832" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33832" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="33834" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="33836" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a><a id="33841" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="33843" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="33845" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="33846" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33846" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="33848" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="33850" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4109" class="Datatype">Value</a><a id="33855" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="33857" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="33859" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>
<a id="33863" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#33793" class="Function">factor</a> <a id="33870" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33870" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="33872" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33872" class="Bound">uâ€²</a> <a id="33875" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33875" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="33877" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33877" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="33879" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="33881" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#31043" class="Function">all-funs</a> <a id="33890" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33872" class="Bound">uâ€²</a>  <a id="33894" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Product.html#1162" class="Function Operator">Ã—</a>  <a id="33897" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33872" class="Bound">uâ€²</a> <a id="33900" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#29383" class="Function Operator">âŠ†</a> <a id="33902" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33870" class="Bound">u</a>  <a id="33905" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Product.html#1162" class="Function Operator">Ã—</a>  <a id="33908" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#32151" class="Function">â¨†dom</a> <a id="33913" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33872" class="Bound">uâ€²</a> <a id="33916" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="33918" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33875" class="Bound">v</a>  <a id="33921" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Product.html#1162" class="Function Operator">Ã—</a>  <a id="33924" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33877" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="33926" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#4466" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ‘</a> <a id="33928" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#32241" class="Function">â¨†cod</a> <a id="33933" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#33872" class="Bound">uâ€²</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
So the inversion principle for functions can be stated as

      v â†¦ w âŠ‘ u
      ---------------
    â†’ factor u uâ€² v w

We prove the inversion principle for functions by induction on the
derivation of the less-than relation. To make the induction hypothesis
stronger, we broaden the premise `v â†¦ w âŠ‘ u` to `uâ‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚`, and
strengthen the conclusion to say that for _every_ function value
`v â†¦ w âˆˆ uâ‚`, we have that `v â†¦ w` factors `uâ‚‚` into some value `uâ‚ƒ`.

    â†’ uâ‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚
      ------------------------------------------------------
    â†’ âˆ€{v w} â†’ v â†¦ w âˆˆ uâ‚ â†’ Î£[ uâ‚ƒ âˆˆ Value ] factor uâ‚‚ uâ‚ƒ v w


### Inversion of less-than for functions, the case for âŠ‘-trans

The crux of the proof is the case for `âŠ‘-trans`.

    uâ‚ âŠ‘ u   u âŠ‘ uâ‚‚
    --------------- (âŠ‘-trans)
        uâ‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚

By the induction hypothesis for `uâ‚ âŠ‘ u`, we know
that `v â†¦ w factors u into uâ€²`, for some value `uâ€²`,
so we have `all-funs uâ€²` and `uâ€² âŠ† u`.
By the induction hypothesis for `u âŠ‘ uâ‚‚`, we know
that for any `vâ€² â†¦ wâ€² âˆˆ u`, `vâ€² â†¦ wâ€²` factors `uâ‚‚` into `uâ‚ƒ`.
With these facts in hand, we proceed by induction on `uâ€²`
to prove that `(â¨†dom uâ€²) â†¦ (â¨†cod uâ€²)` factors `uâ‚‚` into `uâ‚ƒ`.
We discuss each case of the proof in the text below.

          <a id="36249" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#36189" class="Function">uâ‚‚â€²âŠ†uâ‚‚</a> <a id="36256" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="36257" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#36257" class="Bound">C</a><a id="36258" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="36260" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="36261" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Sum.Base.html#662" class="InductiveConstructor">injâ‚</a> <a id="36266" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#36266" class="Bound">x</a><a id="36267" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="36269" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="36271" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#35814" class="Bound">uâ‚ƒâ‚âŠ†uâ‚‚</a> <a id="36278" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#36266" class="Bound">x</a>
          <a id="36290" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#36189" class="Function">uâ‚‚â€²âŠ†uâ‚‚</a> <a id="36297" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="36298" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#36298" class="Bound">C</a><a id="36299" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="36301" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="36302" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Sum.Base.html#687" class="InductiveConstructor">injâ‚‚</a> <a id="36307" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#36307" class="Bound">y</a><a id="36308" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="36310" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="36312" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#35881" class="Bound">uâ‚ƒâ‚‚âŠ†uâ‚‚</a> <a id="36319" href="plfa.part3.Denotational.html#36307" class="Bound">y</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
* Suppose `uâ€² â‰¡ âŠ¥`. Then we have a contradiction because
  it is not the case that `Fun âŠ¥`.

* Suppose `uâ€² â‰¡ uâ‚â€² â†¦ uâ‚‚â€²`. Then `uâ‚â€² â†¦ uâ‚‚â€² âˆˆ u` and we can apply the
  premise (the induction hypothesis from `u âŠ‘ uâ‚‚`) to obtain that
  `uâ‚â€² â†¦ uâ‚‚â€²` factors of `uâ‚‚ into uâ‚‚â€²`. This case is complete because
  `â¨†dom uâ€² â‰¡ uâ‚â€²` and `â¨†cod uâ€² â‰¡ uâ‚‚â€²`.

* Suppose `uâ€² â‰¡ uâ‚â€² âŠ” uâ‚‚â€²`. Then we have `uâ‚â€² âŠ† u` and `uâ‚‚â€² âŠ† u`. We also
  have `all-funs uâ‚â€²` and `all-funs uâ‚‚â€²`, so we can apply the induction hypothesis
  for both `uâ‚â€²` and `uâ‚‚â€²`. So there exists values `uâ‚ƒâ‚` and `uâ‚ƒâ‚‚` such that
  `(â¨†dom uâ‚â€²) â†¦ (â¨†cod uâ‚â€²)` factors `u` into `uâ‚ƒâ‚` and
  `(â¨†dom uâ‚‚â€²) â†¦ (â¨†cod uâ‚‚â€²)` factors `u` into `uâ‚ƒâ‚‚`.
  We will show that `(â¨†dom u) â†¦ (â¨†cod u)` factors `u` into `uâ‚ƒâ‚ âŠ” uâ‚ƒâ‚‚`.
  So we need to show that

        â¨†dom (uâ‚ƒâ‚ âŠ” uâ‚ƒâ‚‚) âŠ‘ â¨†dom (uâ‚â€² âŠ” uâ‚‚â€²)
        â¨†cod (uâ‚â€² âŠ” uâ‚‚â€²) âŠ‘ â¨†cod (uâ‚ƒâ‚ âŠ” uâ‚ƒâ‚‚)

  But those both follow directly from the factoring of
  `u` into `uâ‚ƒâ‚` and `uâ‚ƒâ‚‚`, using the monotonicity of `âŠ”` with respect to `âŠ‘`.


### Inversion of less-than for functions

We come to the proof of the main lemma concerning the inversion of
less-than for functions. We show that if `uâ‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚`, then for any
`v â†¦ w âˆˆ uâ‚`, we can factor `uâ‚‚` into `uâ‚ƒ` according to `v â†¦ w`. We proceed
by induction on the derivation of `uâ‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚`, and describe each case in
the text after the Agda proof.

</pre>{% endraw %}
Let `v` and `w` be arbitrary values.

* Case `âŠ‘-bot`. So `uâ‚ â‰¡ âŠ¥`. We have `v â†¦ w âˆˆ âŠ¥`, but that is impossible.

* Case `âŠ‘-conj-L`.

        uâ‚â‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚   uâ‚â‚‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚
        -------------------
        uâ‚â‚ âŠ” uâ‚â‚‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚

  Given that `v â†¦ w âˆˆ uâ‚â‚ âŠ” uâ‚â‚‚`, there are two subcases to consider.

  * Subcase `v â†¦ w âˆˆ uâ‚â‚`. We conclude by the induction
    hypothesis for `uâ‚â‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚`.

  * Subcase `v â†¦ w âˆˆ uâ‚â‚‚`. We conclude by the induction hypothesis
    for `uâ‚â‚‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚`.

* Case `âŠ‘-conj-R1`.

        uâ‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚â‚
        --------------
        uâ‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚â‚ âŠ” uâ‚‚â‚‚

  Given that `v â†¦ w âˆˆ uâ‚`, the induction hypothesis for `uâ‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚â‚`
  gives us that `v â†¦ w` factors `uâ‚‚â‚` into `uâ‚ƒâ‚` for some `uâ‚ƒâ‚`.
  To show that `v â†¦ w` also factors `uâ‚‚â‚ âŠ” uâ‚‚â‚‚` into `uâ‚ƒâ‚`,
  we just need to show that `uâ‚ƒâ‚ âŠ† uâ‚‚â‚ âŠ” uâ‚‚â‚‚`, but that follows
  directly from `uâ‚ƒâ‚ âŠ† uâ‚‚â‚`.

* Case `âŠ‘-conj-R2`. This case follows by reasoning similar to
  the case for `âŠ‘-conj-R1`.

* Case `âŠ‘-trans`.

        uâ‚ âŠ‘ u   u âŠ‘ uâ‚‚
        ---------------
            uâ‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚

  By the induction hypothesis for `uâ‚ âŠ‘ u`, we know
  that `v â†¦ w` factors `u` into `uâ€²`, for some value `uâ€²`,
  so we have `all-funs uâ€²` and `uâ€² âŠ† u`.
  By the induction hypothesis for `u âŠ‘ uâ‚‚`, we know
  that for any `vâ€² â†¦ wâ€² âˆˆ u`, `vâ€² â†¦ wâ€²` factors `uâ‚‚`.
  Now we apply the lemma sub-inv-trans, which gives us
  some `uâ‚ƒ` such that `(â¨†dom uâ€²) â†¦ (â¨†cod uâ€²)` factors `uâ‚‚` into `uâ‚ƒ`.
  We show that `v â†¦ w` also factors `uâ‚‚` into `uâ‚ƒ`.
  From `â¨†dom uâ‚ƒ âŠ‘ â¨†dom uâ€²` and `â¨†dom uâ€² âŠ‘ v`, we have `â¨†dom uâ‚ƒ âŠ‘ v`.
  From `w âŠ‘ â¨†cod uâ€²` and `â¨†cod uâ€² âŠ‘ â¨†cod uâ‚ƒ`, we have `w âŠ‘ â¨†cod uâ‚ƒ`,
  and this case is complete.

* Case `âŠ‘-fun`.

        uâ‚‚â‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚â‚  uâ‚â‚‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚â‚‚
        ---------------------
        uâ‚â‚ â†¦ uâ‚â‚‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚â‚ â†¦ uâ‚‚â‚‚

  Given that `v â†¦ w âˆˆ uâ‚â‚ â†¦ uâ‚â‚‚`, we have `v â‰¡ uâ‚â‚` and `w â‰¡ uâ‚â‚‚`.
  We show that `uâ‚â‚ â†¦ uâ‚â‚‚` factors `uâ‚‚â‚ â†¦ uâ‚‚â‚‚` into itself.
  We need to show that `â¨†dom (uâ‚‚â‚ â†¦ uâ‚‚â‚‚) âŠ‘ uâ‚â‚` and `uâ‚â‚‚ âŠ‘ â¨†cod (uâ‚‚â‚ â†¦ uâ‚‚â‚‚)`,
  but that is equivalent to our premises `uâ‚‚â‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚â‚` and `uâ‚â‚‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚â‚‚`.

* Case `âŠ‘-dist`.

        ---------------------------------------------
        uâ‚‚â‚ â†¦ (uâ‚‚â‚‚ âŠ” uâ‚‚â‚ƒ) âŠ‘ (uâ‚‚â‚ â†¦ uâ‚‚â‚‚) âŠ” (uâ‚‚â‚ â†¦ uâ‚‚â‚ƒ)

  Given that `v â†¦ w âˆˆ uâ‚‚â‚ â†¦ (uâ‚‚â‚‚ âŠ” uâ‚‚â‚ƒ)`, we have `v â‰¡ uâ‚‚â‚`
  and `w â‰¡ uâ‚‚â‚‚ âŠ” uâ‚‚â‚ƒ`.
  We show that `uâ‚‚â‚ â†¦ (uâ‚‚â‚‚ âŠ” uâ‚‚â‚ƒ)` factors `(uâ‚‚â‚ â†¦ uâ‚‚â‚‚) âŠ” (uâ‚‚â‚ â†¦ uâ‚‚â‚ƒ)`
  into itself. We have `uâ‚‚â‚ âŠ” uâ‚‚â‚ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚â‚`, and also
  `uâ‚‚â‚‚ âŠ” uâ‚‚â‚ƒ âŠ‘ uâ‚‚â‚‚ âŠ” uâ‚‚â‚ƒ`, so the proof is complete.


We conclude this section with two corollaries of the sub-inv lemma.
First, we have the following property that is convenient to use in
later proofs. We specialize the premise to just `v â†¦ w âŠ‘ uâ‚`
and we modify the conclusion to say that for every
`vâ€² â†¦ wâ€² âˆˆ uâ‚‚`, we have `vâ€² âŠ‘ v`.

</pre>{% endraw %}
The second corollary is the inversion rule that one would expect for
less-than with functions on the left and right-hand sides.

## Notes

The denotational semantics presented in this chapter is an example of
a _filter model_ (Barendregt, Coppo, Dezani-Ciancaglini, 1983). Filter
models use type systems with intersection types to precisely
characterize runtime behavior (Coppo, Dezani-Ciancaglini, and Salle,
1979). The notation that we use in this chapter is not that of type
systems and intersection types, but the `Value` data type is isomorphic
to types (`â†¦` is `â†’`, `âŠ”` is `âˆ§`, `âŠ¥` is `âŠ¤`), the `âŠ‘` relation is the
inverse of subtyping `<:`, and the evaluation relation `Ï âŠ¢ M â†“ v` is
isomorphic to a type system. Write `Î“` instead of `Ï`, `A` instead of `v`, and
replace `â†“` with `:` and one has a typing judgement `Î“ âŠ¢ M : A`.
By varying the definition of subtyping and using different choices of
type atoms, intersection type systems provide semantics for many different
untyped Î» calculi, from full beta to the lazy and call-by-value calculi
(Alessi, Barbanera, and Dezani-Ciancaglini, 2006) (Rocca and Paolini, 2004).
The denotational semantics in this chapter corresponds to the BCD
system (Barendregt, Coppo, Dezani-Ciancaglini, 1983).  Part 3 of the
book _Lambda Calculus with Types_ describes a framework for
intersection type systems that enables results similar to the ones in
this chapter, but for the entire family of intersection type systems
(Barendregt, Dekkers, and Statman, 2013).

The two ideas of using finite tables to represent functions and of
relaxing table lookup to enable self application first appeared in a
technical report by Gordon Plotkin (1972) and are later described in
an article in Theoretical Computer Science (Plotkin 1993).  In that
work, the inductive definition of `Value` is a bit different than the
one we use:

    Value = C + â„˜f(Value) Ã— â„˜f(Value)

where `C` is a set of constants and `â„˜f` means finite powerset.  The
pairs in `â„˜f(Value) Ã— â„˜f(Value)` represent input-output mappings, just
as in this chapter. The finite powersets are used to enable a function
table to appear in the input and in the output. These differences
amount to changing where the recursion appears in the definition of
`Value`.  Plotkin's model is an example of a _graph model_ of the
untyped lambda calculus (Barendregt, 1984). In a graph model, the
semantics is presented as a function from programs and environments to
(possibly infinite) sets of values. The semantics in this chapter is
instead defined as a relation, but set-valued functions are isomorphic
to relations. Indeed, we present the semantics as a function in the
next chapter and prove that it is equivalent to the relational
version.

Dana Scott's â„˜(Ï‰) (1976) and Engeler's B(A) (1981) are two more
examples of graph models. Both use the following inductive definition
of `Value`.

    Value = C + â„˜f(Value) Ã— Value

The use of `Value` instead of `â„˜f(Value)` in the output does not restrict
expressiveness compared to Plotkin's model because the semantics use
sets of values and a pair of sets `(V, Vâ€²)` can be represented as a set
of pairs `{ (V, vâ€²) | vâ€² âˆˆ Vâ€² }`.  In Scott's â„˜(Ï‰), the above values are
mapped to and from the natural numbers using a kind of Godel encoding.

  Barbanera, and Mariangiola Dezani-Ciancaglini, Theoretical
  Compututer Science, vol. 355, pages 108-126, 2006.

* The Lambda Calculus. H.P. Barendregt, 1984.

* A filter lambda model and the completeness of type assignment.  Henk
  Barendregt, Mario Coppo, and Mariangiola Dezani-Ciancaglini, Journal
  of Symbolic Logic, vol. 48, pages 931-940, 1983.

* Lambda Calculus with Types. Henk Barendregt, Wil Dekkers, and
  Richard Statman, Cambridge University Press, Perspectives in Logic,
  2013.

* Functional characterization of some semantic equalities inside
  Î»-calculus. Mario Coppo, Mariangiola Dezani-Ciancaglini, and Patrick
  Salle, in Sixth Colloquium on Automata, Languages and Programming.
  Springer, pages 133--146, 1979.

* Algebras and combinators. Erwin Engeler, Algebra Universalis,
  vol. 13, pages 389-392, 1981.

* A Set-Theoretical Definition of Application. Gordon D. Plotkin,
  University of Edinburgh, Technical Report MIP-R-95, 1972.

* Set-theoretical and other elementary models of the Î»-calculus.
  Gordon D. Plotkin, Theoretical Computer Science, vol. 121,
  pages 351-409, 1993.

* The Parametric Lambda Calculus. Simona Ronchi Della Rocca and Luca
  Paolini, Springer, 2004.

* Data Types as Lattices. Dana Scott, SIAM Journal on Computing,
  vol. 5, pages 522-587, 1976.
